  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3e5a29c3-d2d7-4014-ad68-484ccb849020'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi Gabby! I'm currently reading this book right now and as an Alistair Maclean fan I would honestly say this is one of his best behind Ice Station Zeb<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi Gabby! I'm currently reading this book right now and as an Alistair Maclean fan I would honestly say this is one of his best behind Ice Station Zebra (that's my favorite of his). I personally haven't read the two you suggested there. (I really want to though. I just have to find a copy of them! Lol!) Anyway, I think you'll really enjoy this book and also be sure to read Ice Station Zebra if you haven't already. If you would like some more Alistair Maclean suggestions I'd be more than happy to help out. Enjoy! <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <a title="Ian G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/102468787-ian-g"><img alt="Ian G" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579307611p2/102468787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3138863484?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian G" href="/user/show/102468787-ian-g">Ian G</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006157502" href="/book/show/3214291-the-satan-bug">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/102468787-ian-g?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3138863484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11508438074163516763">3.0 ⭐<br/><br/>A serviceable thriller from MacLean, one of his earlier books and one of the better ones. A tough guy investigator/security agent has to recover stolen vials of bio warfare bugs that could wipe out all life, etc., etc. Seems old hat now, because we've seen it so many times, since.This book was written in 1962 and pioneered the concept of bioterrorism in popular culture. It wasn't the first ever novel along those lines but was the first bestseller and was (loosely) turned into a movie of the</span>
  <span id="freeText11508438074163516763" style="display:none">3.0 ⭐<br /><br />A serviceable thriller from MacLean, one of his earlier books and one of the better ones. A tough guy investigator/security agent has to recover stolen vials of bio warfare bugs that could wipe out all life, etc., etc. Seems old hat now, because we've seen it so many times, since.This book was written in 1962 and pioneered the concept of bioterrorism in popular culture. It wasn't the first ever novel along those lines but was the first bestseller and was (loosely) turned into a movie of the same name a few years later.<br /><br />The novel's a kind of hybrid, part detective story with a James Bond finish. It lacks Fleming's stylishness, however, going for a gritter, updated, Bulldog Drummond or Mickey Spillane approach. A lot of whiskey is consumed. While it's dated in its references and language and attitudes it holds up well enough as a beach book type diversion. Many awkward similes. It's a 'Dad' book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11508438074163516763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/663118787?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/6043535-sandy">Sandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer663118787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6444280314899733949">Up until recently, my only experience with Scottish author Alistair MacLean's ninth novel, 1962's "The Satan Bug," was via the film that was loosely made from it three years later. It has long surprised me that this picture--despite featuring two of my favorite performers, Anne Francis and Richard Basehart--is a rather pedestrian, somewhat dull affair, and on the whole, a fairly unmemorable experience. (To be completely honest, it's been quite a while since I have seen the film, and DO need to s</span>
  <span id="freeText6444280314899733949" style="display:none">Up until recently, my only experience with Scottish author Alistair MacLean's ninth novel, 1962's "The Satan Bug," was via the film that was loosely made from it three years later. It has long surprised me that this picture--despite featuring two of my favorite performers, Anne Francis and Richard Basehart--is a rather pedestrian, somewhat dull affair, and on the whole, a fairly unmemorable experience. (To be completely honest, it's been quite a while since I have seen the film, and DO need to see it again soon to refresh my memory.) MacLean's source novel, as it turns out, is a wholly different proposition entirely. Set during two particularly cold and rainy October days in Wiltshire and London, as opposed to the film's sunny California desert, the book is as gripping, suspenseful and exciting as any reader could wish for; simply stated, it is a compulsively readable page-turner. Released just a year before MacLean's slam-bang "Ice Station Zebra," it amply demonstrates that the great thriller writer was surely on some kind of a roll at this point in his career.<br /><br /> In the book, the reader makes the acquaintance of Pierre Cavell, the former head of security at the Mordon (I love that name, with its almost subliminal suggestion of death!) Microbiological Research Establishment, and now working as a private detective. Cavell is handed the case of his life when Mordon's current security chief is found murdered on-site, one of its head scientists disappears...and eight vials containing deadly botulinus toxin AND the so-called Satan Bug (a strain of the polio virus that has been made a million times more deadly, a single spoonful of which could shortly wipe out all life on Earth!) are discovered to be missing! When one of the botulinus vials is released over a section of Norfolk, killing hundreds of animals and people, Cavell realizes that this cunning but maniacal thief certainly does mean business indeed. And as the clock ticks down to an attack on the heart of London, matters grow even more dire for Cavell, as his beautiful bride of just two months is abducted by the madman....<br /><br /> "The Satan Bug," for its first 2/3, comes off almost like a cross between Jacques Futrelle and Agatha Christie, with Cavell evincing the sharp ratiocination abilities of The Thinking Machine and Hercule Poirot; in its final third, the novel dishes out some tremendous chase and action sequences. Cavell, during this case, must sift through the alibis of a good two dozen or so Mordon suspects, and every character, it seems, has something to hide. It is the sort of book in which no one can be trusted; where virtually everyone is playacting or double-dealing for his or her own end...even the "good guys." Cavell goes through some fairly physically grueling treatment during the course of his 48-hour investigation, and it is no small wonder that he emerges both alive at the book's end and that he is able to figure out the culprit in this very complexly plotted affair. Like so many of MacLean's other action leads, Cavell impresses the reader with both his mental agility AND his ability to carry on against near insuperable odds. The book features much in the way of surprises (Cavell's exact relationship with his boss, The General, did surely catch me off guard!), and as far as the reader's ability to figure out the identity of the culprit...well, my advice would be to not even try; just sit back and marvel as Cavell blunders and divines his way closer to the truth. The novel also features any number of stunning set pieces, such as when one of the Mordon scientists, Dr. Gregori, tells us in some detail what the Satan Bug is capable of; a nasty fight that Cavell has with the madman's mute henchman, Henriques, on a high fire escape and then amongst the interior roof girders of an enormous railway building; and the absolutely thrilling sequence in which Cavell, close to physical collapse and sporting several broken ribs, must duke it out with the killer in a bucking helicopter high above London. (The film also featured a helicopter climax, but in a completely different context.) I found the book absolutely riveting, both the detective section and the thrilling denouement, and feel that it should greatly please just about any reader.<br /><br /> Having said that, I must also report that "The Satan Bug" is not a perfect book, and that MacLean can justly be accused of having made a few flubs during the course of his complicated story. Most egregiously, a character named Tom Hartnell on page 75 (I refer here to the classic Fawcett Gold Medal edition of the mid-'60s; the book is currently available in a nice-looking Sterling edition) is called Roger Hartnell by page 128! MacLean tells us that the city of Tornio is in Sweden, whereas it is actually in Finland, on the Swedish border. A fictitious town called Lower Hampton (in Norfolk, where the botulinus toxin is released) is shortly after referred to as Little Hampton. And finally, at one point, Cavell questions a man in a doorway who "leaned a shoulder against the lintel." But since a lintel is the overhead support ABOVE a doorway, I'm not sure how any person could physically lean against it! I can only assume that the author meant "doorjamb" here. But these are mere quibbles; some minor boo-boos that should have been caught by MacLean's editor. The bottom line is that the book is a smashing success, and some kind of pure entertainment. "The Satan Bug," by the way, was initially released under MacLean's pseudonym of Ian Stuart, just to see if one of his books would sell successfully under another byline. It did, of course, but with a thriller like this, that should hardly come as a surprise....</span>
  <a data-text-id="6444280314899733949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_194645110" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194645110" />
    <a title="Checkman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5117003-checkman"><img alt="Checkman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591798821p2/5117003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194645110?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Checkman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Checkman" href="/user/show/5117003-checkman">Checkman</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12285991-the-satan-bug">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of thrillers and MacLean</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=detective">detective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=beach-read">beach-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=espionage">espionage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer194645110&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194645110" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4150756819533957147">Okay so it's not one of Mr. MacLean's stronger novels, but it works. It works. Yes it's what would now be known as a "mashup" with all the attending flaws of those books. It crosses into different genres. Detective, mystery, espionage and thriller and as a result is a bit muddled at times. I've read that with this novel (which MacLean originally wrote under the pen-name Ian Stuart) he was trying to see if he could write a hard-boiled detective novel. For whatever reason he decided to write under</span>
  <span id="freeText4150756819533957147" style="display:none">Okay so it's not one of Mr. MacLean's stronger novels, but it works. It works. Yes it's what would now be known as a "mashup" with all the attending flaws of those books. It crosses into different genres. Detective, mystery, espionage and thriller and as a result is a bit muddled at times. I've read that with this novel (which MacLean originally wrote under the pen-name Ian Stuart) he was trying to see if he could write a hard-boiled detective novel. For whatever reason he decided to write under an alias. <br /><br />Approximately a third of the way through the book Alistair MacLean emerges and the book steers back into his territory.Espionage, double-crosses (also triple), red herrings and thrills and chills. It's not a bad novel. Like I said earlier it works. Take it to the beach. Take it to the pool so you have something to do when the kids are splashing around. It will burn the time. What more can you ask for from this type of novel? I've read it a couple times now. Oh ,and I hope I'm not giving anything away here, but the bad guys don't get away with it, the damsel is rescued and the world is saved.<br /><br />Made into a movie by Hollywood in 1965. The story is moved to the desert of Southern California, but is fairly faithful to the source material otherwise. The movie was directed by the always dependable John Sturges who would follow-up with the movie adaptation of <i>Ice Station Zebra</i> in 1968. It's worth a look.</span>

  <span id="freeText6360548735184326553" style="display:none">Top class thriller. Alistair Maclean was the master of suspense and thrill. I had almost forgotten this book, but after reviewing The Golden Rendezvous and The Last Frontier, I thought I would look up the list of Alistair Maclean books and lo and behold, I found this book - which I had completely forgotten. <br /><br />I was young when I read this book, I mean a young teenager. I don't have to see a Maclean movie - his books stir the imagination in a way that is impossible to describe. You can actually SEE things happening. Such a vivid writer. </span>

<div id="review_303454829" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/303454829" />
    <a title="Rich Cook" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5226614-rich-cook"><img alt="Rich Cook" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333214900p2/5226614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/303454829?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rich Cook" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rich Cook" href="/user/show/5226614-rich-cook">Rich Cook</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer303454829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11308664373344898658">Not his best work but a fun and easy read. The ending or final act, from the second plot point, is a study in how to write a ripping good ending. The hero figures something out but the villain out wits him. The hero gets an edge; the villain is better. That repeats at least 20 times until the hero finally gets the edge. Excellent.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review303454829">

<div id="review_1258911358" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1258911358" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30916346-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398654686p2/30916346.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1258911358?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/30916346-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006157502" href="/book/show/3214291-the-satan-bug">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30916346-diane?shelf=thriller-and-crime">thriller-and-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1258911358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10491834404338661898">This is the first novel that I have read by Alistar MacLean. My previous exposure to him was the movie, "Ice Station Zebra," which is one of my favorites. My father has a pile of these books that he hasn't read in some time, so I borrowed a couple (this one and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/149656.Bear_Island' title='Bear Island by Alistair MacLean' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bear Island</a>). <br/><br/>"The Satan Bug" is a great mix of adventure, espionage, and mystery. Pierre Clavell, half-French/half-English, served with the British Army during World War II, joined the police and rose to Inspector, and then worked as the</span>
  <span id="freeText10491834404338661898" style="display:none">This is the first novel that I have read by Alistar MacLean. My previous exposure to him was the movie, "Ice Station Zebra," which is one of my favorites. My father has a pile of these books that he hasn't read in some time, so I borrowed a couple (this one and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/149656.Bear_Island" title="Bear Island by Alistair MacLean" rel="nofollow noopener">Bear Island</a>). <br /><br />"The Satan Bug" is a great mix of adventure, espionage, and mystery. Pierre Clavell, half-French/half-English, served with the British Army during World War II, joined the police and rose to Inspector, and then worked as the head of security at Mordon Labs, a high security scientific facility that secretly specialized in the development of deadly germ toxins. Fired from this last job, Clavell is trying to make it as a private detective, but there are no takers - until one day the mysterious Henry Martin shows up with a proposition for him. Despite the high security at Mordon, someone has managed to murder Clavell's replacement as security head and the director, Dr Baxter, has mysteriously vanished. Later they discover that deadly botulinus (botulism) and the even deadlier "Satan Bug" have been stolen. The "Satan Bug" has the power to kill a million people very quickly - and someone is threatening to use it. <br /><br />There are a lot of twists and turns in the plot. Just when you think you know what's going on, it gets turned around and you realize you were wrong. I was surprised by how much detection goes on because I was expecting more of an adventure book. Since I am a mystery fanatic, this is one of the reasons I enjoyed "The Satan Bug" so much. The book is fast-paced and only 256 pages long, so it's a quick read. It took me longer because I was working overtime and didn't have as much free time for reading. A pet peeve of mine is overly long mysteries or thrillers. A lot of the time, they're just padding. "The Satan Bug" is not. <br /><br />A very enjoyable read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10491834404338661898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_852615562" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/852615562" />
    <a title="Philip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7413069-philip"><img alt="Philip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583291726p2/7413069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/852615562?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Philip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Philip" href="/user/show/7413069-philip">Philip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006157502" href="/book/show/3214291-the-satan-bug">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7413069-philip?shelf=mystery-thriller-crime">mystery-thriller-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7413069-philip?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7413069-philip?shelf=1960s">1960s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7413069-philip?shelf=kiss-kiss-bang-bang">kiss-kiss-bang-bang</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7413069-philip?shelf=first-person">first-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7413069-philip?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer852615562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2406815253034995507">Interesting to see that biological weapons were as much of a threat 50 years ago as they are today. SPOILER ALERT: The actual "Satan Bug" is largely a MacGuffin here for what is basically a whodunit with a little action at the end, rather than an espionage or political thriller. This is also the second MacLean book I know of where the defeated bad guy chooses the "honorable" path and kills himself by jumping out of a plane rather than face trial - not sure if this is some quaint British code of </span>
  <span id="freeText2406815253034995507" style="display:none">Interesting to see that biological weapons were as much of a threat 50 years ago as they are today. SPOILER ALERT: The actual "Satan Bug" is largely a MacGuffin here for what is basically a whodunit with a little action at the end, rather than an espionage or political thriller. This is also the second MacLean book I know of where the defeated bad guy chooses the "honorable" path and kills himself by jumping out of a plane rather than face trial - not sure if this is some quaint British code of honor from that period.<br /><br />This book is still from MacLean's "good period," before he started going downhill after <b>Force 10</b>. I've now somehow read most of them the past year or so, but this should be it for a while - no more from Mom and none at the library except a few of his final works which were generally pretty bad. Still have never read <b>HMS Ulysses</b> or <b>South by Java Head,</b> and would like to sometime - but they're not available in Singapore so will have to wait until we get back to Virginia someday.<br /><br />BTW, like so many of MacLean's books, this was turned into a movie - but one of his "lesser works" starring mainly TV actors (George Maharis, Richard Basehart, Anne Francis) rather than the true movie stars that worked on the better adaptations, such as "Guns of Navarone," "Where Eagles Dare" and "Ice Station Zebra." That said, an interesting bit of trivia is that the "Satan Bug" script was co-written by James Clavell, before he made it big as an author with <b>Shogun</b> and <b>Tai-Pan</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2406815253034995507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2973094389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13857592922053779979">"The Satan Bug" is a historical thriller about bioterrorism. Mordon Research Centre is a secret and well-guarded research lab. However, one night behind its secured walls, a scientist found dead. At first, they were not sure was it murder or suicide until they found out a deadly virus had disappeared. Cavell Investigations caught the case due to the owner's connection to the facility. The readers of The Satan Bug will continue to follow Cavell Investigations to find out what happens.<br/><br/>"The Satan B</span>
  <span id="freeText13857592922053779979" style="display:none">"The Satan Bug" is a historical thriller about bioterrorism. Mordon Research Centre is a secret and well-guarded research lab. However, one night behind its secured walls, a scientist found dead. At first, they were not sure was it murder or suicide until they found out a deadly virus had disappeared. Cavell Investigations caught the case due to the owner's connection to the facility. The readers of The Satan Bug will continue to follow Cavell Investigations to find out what happens.<br /><br />"The Satan Bug" is another fantastic book by Alistair MacLean. I like the way Alistair MacLean portrayed his characters and the way they interact with each other. The Satan Bug was well written and researched by Alistair Maclean. Alistair MacLean did an excellent job of describing the settings of The Satan Bug.<br /><br />The readers of The Satan Bug will learn about the problem people have who can not handle authority. Also, the readers of The Satan Bug will start to understand the using poisons to kill someone is a painful way to die for the person that you poisoned. <br /><br />I recommend this book. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />I recommend this book.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3241964482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4237898145841428816">Great mystery thriller with nonstop action and suspenseful plot twists. Alistair Maclean was a master storyteller.<br/>But most of all don't miss the film version (1965) loosely based on this novel by Mr Maclean (with a very good screenplay by James Clavell & Edward Anhalt).<br/>Directed with great skill by John Sturges ("Bad Day at Black Rock", "Gunfight at O.K. Corral" and many more), with a wonderful cast (Richard Basehart, Annie Francis, Dana Andrews, John Anderson, Ed Asner, George Maharis, among oth</span>
  <span id="freeText4237898145841428816" style="display:none">Great mystery thriller with nonstop action and suspenseful plot twists. Alistair Maclean was a master storyteller.<br />But most of all don't miss the film version (1965) loosely based on this novel by Mr Maclean (with a very good screenplay by James Clavell &amp; Edward Anhalt).<br />Directed with great skill by John Sturges ("Bad Day at Black Rock", "Gunfight at O.K. Corral" and many more), with a wonderful cast (Richard Basehart, Annie Francis, Dana Andrews, John Anderson, Ed Asner, George Maharis, among others), a nice cinematography (by Robert Surtees) and a perfect music score by the late great Jerry Goldsmith. <br />"The Satan Bug" is one of those rare examples of an excellent book and an even better film adaptation.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2454864145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2454864145" />
    <a title="Neil Fulwood" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78510209-neil-fulwood"><img alt="Neil Fulwood" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520021486p2/78510209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2454864145?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil Fulwood" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil Fulwood" href="/user/show/78510209-neil-fulwood">Neil Fulwood</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006157502" href="/book/show/3214291-the-satan-bug">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2454864145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14139017407757838314">The second of two novels MacLean originally published under the pseudonym Ian Stuart - the other one being ‘The Dark Crusader’- ‘The Satan Bug’ boasts a particularly lurid title and an equally lurid premise: a break-in and a double murder at a top secret government facility dedicated to chemical warfare research sees the institute’s former security director, the grizzled, sarcastic and brutally efficient Pierre Cavell, drawn back into the fold. Published pseudonymously it might have been, but th</span>
  <span id="freeText14139017407757838314" style="display:none">The second of two novels MacLean originally published under the pseudonym Ian Stuart - the other one being ‘The Dark Crusader’- ‘The Satan Bug’ boasts a particularly lurid title and an equally lurid premise: a break-in and a double murder at a top secret government facility dedicated to chemical warfare research sees the institute’s former security director, the grizzled, sarcastic and brutally efficient Pierre Cavell, drawn back into the fold. Published pseudonymously it might have been, but this is pure MacLean: the hero as dark horse, the traitor in the midst, hidden agendas, duplicitous dealings, and more twists and turns than a very twisty thing that’s just graduated with honours from the twisty-turny university. Stylistically, it starts off almost as a police procedural before leaping into thriller territory. By the last quarter, the big action set pieces that MacLean is famous for are being tossed out left, right and centre. The sudden lurch from procedural to action thriller is a bit jarring and unsubtle, but that’s my only real criticism. Otherwise, this is one hell of a pacy read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14139017407757838314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2100556917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2100556917" />
    <a title="Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58230784-sue"><img alt="Sue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584694505p2/58230784.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2100556917?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue" href="/user/show/58230784-sue">Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006157502" href="/book/show/3214291-the-satan-bug">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2100556917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16935551750988431903">For a 'near classic' I was expecting more. Alistair Maclean's tale of espionage, kidnapping, a couple of deadly 'bugs' in colour-coded flasks and a secret laboratory facility did keep me reading to the very end but there was too much that was unbelievable. The confusion between virus, bacteria and toxin was annoying - the words were used interchangeably (OK, google wasn't around when this was written but they had encyclopaedias... perhaps Maclean thought his readers would not know or care). Also</span>
  <span id="freeText16935551750988431903" style="display:none">For a 'near classic' I was expecting more. Alistair Maclean's tale of espionage, kidnapping, a couple of deadly 'bugs' in colour-coded flasks and a secret laboratory facility did keep me reading to the very end but there was too much that was unbelievable. The confusion between virus, bacteria and toxin was annoying - the words were used interchangeably (OK, google wasn't around when this was written but they had encyclopaedias... perhaps Maclean thought his readers would not know or care). Also, all biologists know that 'bugs' are insects and would only ever call a micro-organism a 'bug' for a joke.<br /><br />The bad guy's rise to a position of prominence was totally ridiculous - he would have been spotted as a fraud within hours. The book is probably just a product of its time though. All the men had aggressive, petulant, belligerent or truculent attitudes which became annoying and monotonous after a while. There were only around 3-4 female characters, all with minor roles.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16935551750988431903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer63376782533565610">Private investigator Pierre Cavell is called in to solve the mystery of who robbed the Mordon Microbiological Research Center, a government research lab in England which develops synthetic viruses. The thieves took a deadly virus codenamed the Satan Bug, and it's up to Cavell to find them and recover the virus before it's unleashed.<br/><br/>Up 'till this book, I'd only been familiar with author Alistair MacLean's World War II-themed works such as The Guns of Navarone and Where Eagles Dare. The Satan Bug </span>
  <span id="freeText63376782533565610" style="display:none">Private investigator Pierre Cavell is called in to solve the mystery of who robbed the Mordon Microbiological Research Center, a government research lab in England which develops synthetic viruses. The thieves took a deadly virus codenamed the Satan Bug, and it's up to Cavell to find them and recover the virus before it's unleashed.<br /><br />Up 'till this book, I'd only been familiar with author Alistair MacLean's World War II-themed works such as The Guns of Navarone and Where Eagles Dare. The Satan Bug was a very pleasant surprise. While it's a little slow to get going, once MacLean gets Cavell to Mordon things really pick up and almost never let up. There's lots of tension, twists and turns, and the revelation of who the evil mastermind is was quite a surprise!</span>

She's super pretty, helpful and serves primarily as a hostage. She was played in the 1965 movie by Anne Francis, who made a lengthy career out of screaming when grabbed by the bad guy / monster / whatever.   <span id="freeText6765105342945546901" style="display:none">Pretty much by the numbers Alistair MacLean suspense except this time the loner hero is a married loner.<br />But don't worry, Mary doesn't actually have a character. She was played in the 1965 movie by Anne Francis, who made a lengthy career out of screaming when grabbed by the bad guy / monster / whatever. She squeezed tapings of "Satan Bug" in between three episodes of the "Alfred Hitchcock Hour" and "Brainstorm" (plot synopsis: "Scientist Jim Grayam saves his boss' wife from suicide but falls in-love with her and plots to kill her husband by pretending to be criminally insane."). I'm not sure she could have remembered which role was which.<br />Cliche ridden and kind of dull but not horrible. A low point for MacLean.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8944088780478697068">As always, there are several layers and multiple red herrings in a plot that largely revolves around the theft of virus samples produced for microbiological warfare. As in his stories I've read so far, the tempo picks up right from the start and there's not a moment where it drops speed.<br/>The bad guys in the story are the worst I'v</span>
  <span id="freeText8944088780478697068" style="display:none">As always, there are several layers and multiple red herrings in a plot that largely revolves around the theft of virus samples produced for microbiological warfare. The story starts at the office of Pierre Cavell, shown as a private investigator who it later turns out is a covert agent working for several years under the 'General'. As in his stories I've read so far, the tempo picks up right from the start and there's not a moment where it drops speed.<br />The bad guys in the story are the worst I've seen yet from among his books and reeking of pure evil. I'm rating it with 3 starts because of the somewhat convoluted climax. I felt it a tad too complicated and perhaps unnecessarily elongated for my liking.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer509892586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7545275357978735877">I believe this book was originally released under a pseudonym, Ian Stuart. I only read it for the first time a year or two back. I thought it was good, but not one of MacLean's best. Since then, I have discovered a few reviews and it seems that The Satan Bug is highly-regarded in MacLean circles.<br/><br/>Released in 1962, the novel is about the theft of an indestructible virus that presents a threat to mankind. The only way to stop it is with a typically cynical MacLean hero, Cavell!<br/><br/>Good fun nowadays, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText7545275357978735877" style="display:none">I believe this book was originally released under a pseudonym, Ian Stuart. I only read it for the first time a year or two back. I thought it was good, but not one of MacLean's best. Since then, I have discovered a few reviews and it seems that The Satan Bug is highly-regarded in MacLean circles.<br /><br />Released in 1962, the novel is about the theft of an indestructible virus that presents a threat to mankind. The only way to stop it is with a typically cynical MacLean hero, Cavell!<br /><br />Good fun nowadays, but probably quite pertinent back in '62.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_115562408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115562408" />
    <a title="Stacy Jensen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1871904-stacy-jensen"><img alt="Stacy Jensen" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115562408?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacy Jensen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacy Jensen" href="/user/show/1871904-stacy-jensen">Stacy Jensen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115562408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17644269169755263837">Someone has stolen an extremely dangerous toxin from a secret lab in England. If it gets into the wrong hands, millions of people could die! See, that's why I don't write spy novels. I make them sound cheesy. But this book isn't cheesy. It's by master spy novelist Alistair MacLean, one of my faves from the sixties. I'll probably go on a MacLean reading jag so everything will sound the same for awhile. Sorry.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_336941349" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/336941349" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1256709-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586201432p2/1256709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/336941349?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/1256709-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer336941349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5093780138003412913">I read this years ago and reread it recently after channel-surfing into the 1965 film starring George Maharis and Anne Francis. The movie is entertaining, but Alistair MacClean’s book is far more visceral and fast-paced. Maybe transplanting the plot from the cold, wet UK to sunny Southern California is part of the problem. In any event, read the book if you like a good thriller.<br/><br/>Originally published in 1962 under the pseudonym of Ian Stuart.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2072852956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2072852956" />
    <a title="Oliver Clarke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7902804-oliver-clarke"><img alt="Oliver Clarke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543132959p2/7902804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2072852956?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Oliver Clarke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Oliver Clarke" href="/user/show/7902804-oliver-clarke">Oliver Clarke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006157502" href="/book/show/3214291-the-satan-bug">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2072852956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15949516772597923544">Not as much fun as 'The Guns of Navarone', which I read a couple of months ago, but still an entertaining read. This is really more of a detective story than an adventure, with the hero trying to track down a stolen super virus. It's a little pedestrian at times, with much of the action confined to rural England, but the thrilling climax makes up for it. Even that doesn't quite live up to the promise of the title though. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7130379826588711090">I was a huge fan of MacLean as a kid and teenager. He, along with Jack London and Robert A. Heinlein, were my favorite authors back then. <br/><br/>I wasn't sure what rereading these as an adult would be like. I'm probably not as forgiving for MacLean's verbosity as I was as a kid. And there's certainly some dated gender attitudes. But overall, I'm happy to say that it was still a fun and gripping read. </span>

          </span>

I loved this the first time I read it, and I've read it easily seven or eight times since: Alastair MacLean was one of my favourite authors when I was young, and this is one of his best, particularly of the non-war instalments.</span>

<div id="review_1987096540" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1987096540" />
    <a title="Malcolm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3340373-malcolm"><img alt="Malcolm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267085906p2/3340373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1987096540?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Malcolm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Malcolm" href="/user/show/3340373-malcolm">Malcolm</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006157502" href="/book/show/3214291-the-satan-bug">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3340373-malcolm?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1987096540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3997215933824700828">I recall seeing the film of this novel back in the 1960s, a viewing which first drew my attention to the threat of biological weapons as a form of warfare. While I have learnt a lot about these weapons in the intervening years, I did not add to my knowledge by reading this book. It is a thriller with biological weapons as an element. Worse is that MacLean revisits the plot of this novel in <u> Goodbye California </u> (1978) with atomic bombs and Islamic terrorists taking the place of botulism and anti </span>
  <span id="freeText3997215933824700828" style="display:none">I recall seeing the film of this novel back in the 1960s, a viewing which first drew my attention to the threat of biological weapons as a form of warfare. While I have learnt a lot about these weapons in the intervening years, I did not add to my knowledge by reading this book. It is a thriller with biological weapons as an element. Worse is that MacLean revisits the plot of this novel in <u> Goodbye California </u> (1978) with atomic bombs and Islamic terrorists taking the place of botulism and anti war activists. He even reprises the device of the main character being motivated by the enemy kidnapping his wife.<br />As with most MacLean novels the pace of action is unrelenting. We do not however have a clock ticking at the headline of each chapter. The hero's ability to work without sleep and food is just part of the improbability of his character. He seems to be able to see things which Scotland Yard and the reader, for that matter, can not see and that in spite of the villain's elaborate set of red herrings which would outdo Agatha Christie.<br />It begins like a Phillip Marlowe novel but quickly takes on elements of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16206904.The_Thirty_Nine_Steps__Greenmantle__The_World_s_Best_Reading_" title="The Thirty-Nine Steps. Greenmantle (The World's Best Reading) by John Buchan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thirty-Nine Steps. Greenmantle</a> as the hero escapes his bonds inside a locked basement but finally this is more like Hercule Poirot as our hero seems to be able to guess what is actually happening. Yet there is also something of Bulldog Drummond when our hero chooses to save his country over saving his wife.<br />Unlike modern thriller writers, MacLean does not write down for his readers. I see a serious attempt to write in a style which has some purpose in the narrative. None of Lee Child's short sentences here: "I squirmed around on the floor, picked up the Hanyatti with my bound hands, slipped the safety catch and dragged the gun around to my right side as far as the unnaturally twisted position of my left shoulder would allow." Yet the style can also accommodate description of fast paced action: "we heard a sudden movement outside, the shadow of an arm fell across the side of an embrasure and something came spinning into the room. Something that glittered and flashed in the light from the lamp on the floor. Something made of glass, with a red seal on top. A botulinus ampoule."<br />"botulinus ampoule" is not the only example of a vocabulary which demands a little more from the reader. "a photographic memory for all the more monumental irrelevancies of life." demonstrates the hero's natural way of speaking.<br />It is interesting that the novel first appeared under the name of Ian Stuart, the second with this conceit, although I recall most reviewers at the time knew the identity of the writer. I can only conjecture that MacLean did this to see if his writing would stand up on its own without his name on the cover. As a thriller, the book stands up well, only slightly dated. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3997215933824700828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_844825694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/844825694" />
    <a title="Ant Koplowitz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5001035-ant-koplowitz"><img alt="Ant Koplowitz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507757120p2/5001035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/844825694?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ant Koplowitz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ant Koplowitz" href="/user/show/5001035-ant-koplowitz">Ant Koplowitz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006157502" href="/book/show/3214291-the-satan-bug">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5001035-ant-koplowitz?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer844825694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5852256452185147922">The Satan Bug by Alistair MacLean is an old fashioned spy romp, with an agent sent, somewhat circuitously, to investigate and recover a deadly virus from a top secret chemical research establishment. It's an easy read (although there's a few too many characters and roles to remember, especially at the start of the book) and the pace never lets up, with the action sequences following in quick succession. There's plenty of bluff and double bluff and our virtually omnipresent protagonist always man</span>
  <span id="freeText5852256452185147922" style="display:none">The Satan Bug by Alistair MacLean is an old fashioned spy romp, with an agent sent, somewhat circuitously, to investigate and recover a deadly virus from a top secret chemical research establishment. It's an easy read (although there's a few too many characters and roles to remember, especially at the start of the book) and the pace never lets up, with the action sequences following in quick succession. There's plenty of bluff and double bluff and our virtually omnipresent protagonist always manages to stay just one step ahead of the villains. Not much depth to the characters, and this is action and pace over style and depth. But I enjoyed it...it's escapist, improbable 'nonsense', but tightly plotted and evocative nonsense nevertheless. <br /><br />© Koplowitz 2014</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1358834189" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10869231042093721295">One of two books that MacLean wrote under the pseudonym "Ian Stuart" in the early 60s, supposedly as to prove that his by then established name was not the only thing that made his stories popular. Apparently, he was soon found out and the books issued under his name. Even so, this and "The Dark Crusader" are a bit odd ones out among the extremely well-known titles of his early bibliography. Or maybe I'm imagining that. Either way, this is a suspenseful and effective thriller, with the theft of </span>
  <span id="freeText10869231042093721295" style="display:none">One of two books that MacLean wrote under the pseudonym "Ian Stuart" in the early 60s, supposedly as to prove that his by then established name was not the only thing that made his stories popular. Apparently, he was soon found out and the books issued under his name. Even so, this and "The Dark Crusader" are a bit odd ones out among the extremely well-known titles of his early bibliography. Or maybe I'm imagining that. Either way, this is a suspenseful and effective thriller, with the theft of "The Satan Bug", an extremely deadly virus dreamt up for biological warfare, as backdrop. An OK read, not among his best and certainly not of his worst either. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10510379350196656339"><i>It's pretty good. I would've given it 4 stars had it been some other author</i><br/><br/>In the beginning it's pretty intriguing. It has some great thrills here and there, with a <i>surprisingly believable</i> end-of-the-world plot that you don't see in other books of this sort. Characters are pretty cool, there are some nice twists at the end of some of the chapters.<br/><br/>Now that I think of it, this book has EVERY SINGLE element of a GREAT spy/detective thriller. It's just that the components aren't glued together very </span>
  <span id="freeText10510379350196656339" style="display:none"><i>It's pretty good. I would've given it 4 stars had it been some other author</i><br /><br />In the beginning it's pretty intriguing. It has some great thrills here and there, with a <i>surprisingly believable</i> end-of-the-world plot that you don't see in other books of this sort. Characters are pretty cool, there are some nice twists at the end of some of the chapters.<br /><br />Now that I think of it, this book has EVERY SINGLE element of a GREAT spy/detective thriller. It's just that the components aren't glued together very well.<br /><br /><i>Something, something prison</i>, then <i>something something killing germ</i> then, after a while it's just <i>something something</i></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XYsSrSYivjzjkqiuU4oBgIeYEyJQhV8r4xXxjv11rfxA7nYa5bs31e3WD0As1MERTVqtSKZXICwuHEH6fDQJ4w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pLqil8ty8diL5//FhfhU2iZidMjcVHaDkomUThvtqg+538YgCOt4MYWjWCv6ppRL7KDKoiqGCYRfgCQ6mqwOEA==')})

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26970.Alistair_MacLean">About Alistair MacLean</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13479086457643809205">Alistair Stuart MacLean (Scottish Gaelic: Alasdair MacGill-Eain), the son of a Scots Minister, was brought up in the Scottish Highlands. In 1941, at the age of eighteen, he joined the Royal Navy; two and a half years spent aboard a cruiser were to give him the background for <i>HMS Ulysses</i>, his first novel, the outstanding documentary novel on the war at sea. After the war he gained an English Honour</span>
  <span id="freeText13479086457643809205" style="display:none">Alistair Stuart MacLean (Scottish Gaelic: Alasdair MacGill-Eain), the son of a Scots Minister, was brought up in the Scottish Highlands. In 1941, at the age of eighteen, he joined the Royal Navy; two and a half years spent aboard a cruiser were to give him the background for <i>HMS Ulysses</i>, his first novel, the outstanding documentary novel on the war at sea. After the war he gained an English Honours degree at Glasgow University, and became a schoolmaster. In 1983, he was awarded a D. Litt. from the same university.<br /><br />Maclean is the author of twenty-nine world bestsellers and recognised as an outstanding writer in his own genre. Many of his titles have been adapted for film - <i>The Guns of the Navarone</i>, <i>The Satan Bug</i>, <i>Force Ten from Navarone</i>, <i>Where Eagles Dare</i> and <i>Bear Island</i> are among the most famous. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13479086457643809205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
